<div id="review_4395016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4395016" />
    <a title="Lorena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/251417-lorena"><img alt="Lorena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489184320p2/251417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4395016?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorena" href="/user/show/251417-lorena">Lorena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251417-lorena?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4395016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12269940890376393773">I found the fantasy world that was created here to be very interesting, and the author certainly does like her anti-heroes, based on this book and the one other I've read by her so far. However, I felt that the backstory and some of the characters could have used more filling out. We've barely been introduced to our main characters when suddenly they are thrust into their Designated Quest, supposedly in part because of the deep feelings two of the characters apparently formed for each other virt</span>
  <span id="freeText12269940890376393773" style="display:none">I found the fantasy world that was created here to be very interesting, and the author certainly does like her anti-heroes, based on this book and the one other I've read by her so far. However, I felt that the backstory and some of the characters could have used more filling out. We've barely been introduced to our main characters when suddenly they are thrust into their Designated Quest, supposedly in part because of the deep feelings two of the characters apparently formed for each other virtually overnight. Also, I couldn't tell if one character's Secret Identity was really supposed to be a secret from the reader or not, since it seemed glaringly obvious to me from the beginning, so the unraveling of that particular mystery by the other characters struck me as tedious. Perhaps more of the backstory will be explained in the subsequent books in the series...I'm giving them a chance, at least. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12269940890376393773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_916742522" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer12958263056041740330">Read this trilogy ages ago, before I was even on GR. I've hardly seen it talked about on here which is a shame as although the pacing was poor in places and the supporting cast of characters was limited this was a memorable trilogy (especially this first installment) with one of the most unique and disturbing worlds in fantasy or sci-fi and a great relationship/bromance developed between the 2 lead characters. Gerald Tarrant was also a great anti-hero or maybe just straight up villain. A man who</span>
  <span id="freeText12958263056041740330" style="display:none">Read this trilogy ages ago, before I was even on GR. I've hardly seen it talked about on here which is a shame as although the pacing was poor in places and the supporting cast of characters was limited this was a memorable trilogy (especially this first installment) with one of the most unique and disturbing worlds in fantasy or sci-fi and a great relationship/bromance developed between the 2 lead characters. Gerald Tarrant was also a great anti-hero or maybe just straight up villain. A man who had done truly horrible things and whose motivations for much of the series were far from noble but he was always compelling whenever he appeared throughout the series and his redemption arc in the final book did a lot to humanize him.</span>

<div id="review_318183474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318183474" />
    <a title="Neda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3337077-neda"><img alt="Neda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318171744p2/3337077.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318183474?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neda" href="/user/show/3337077-neda">Neda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3337077-neda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3337077-neda?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3337077-neda?shelf=couldn-t-finish">couldn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318183474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1747085229340280236">I slogged through about half of the book, thinking maybe it will get better - I heard a lot of praises for this trilogy, so I expected something quite different. But I give up. I'm done. No more.<br/>One reason why this book gets two and not one star is the magic system, which is interesting, if confusing - humans can use, consciously or unconsciously, natural forces of the planet Erna (called fae) to, well, do stuff, like materialize fantasies or nightmares, or change reality in accordance to their </span>
  <span id="freeText1747085229340280236" style="display:none">I slogged through about half of the book, thinking maybe it will get better - I heard a lot of praises for this trilogy, so I expected something quite different. But I give up. I'm done. No more.<br />One reason why this book gets two and not one star is the magic system, which is interesting, if confusing - humans can use, consciously or unconsciously, natural forces of the planet Erna (called fae) to, well, do stuff, like materialize fantasies or nightmares, or change reality in accordance to their purpose. So we have quite a different natural world then on Earth - evolution works according to the need of the creature, and humans unknowingly with their research created their rival species on the planet. Not the Star Trek story here - humans immediately tried to commit genocide, causing rakh (said species) to flee and try to protect themselves, creating demons which plague humans. Or something.<br />So, that's the good start.<br />Then we have our main characters - kind of vampire/evil fae/ex-human, priest (faith is the weapon of mass destruction here), chick/ex-adept in magic and kind of sidekick of the said chick go on a quest, searching for stolen...I don't know...adept-ness of the chick (she can't do magic anymore). Ok, good. There is even kind of girl-rakh, though I didn't follow that through. What I don't understand is why every character in this book just have to be so damn unlikable. Every time I kinda try to like somebody, he/she just do something to make me mad (or indifferent, honestly, I didn't think that possible). Or he/she isn't there anymore. I don't like the chick, I don't know why her co-characters like her, and why they want to help her. We don't know anything about her, except some vague things about her vitality, and some flirty stuff whith the priest, all vague. Really. Kind-of-vampire had some promise, but not much charm. Priest has the personality of a brick wall. And sidekick...I almost forgot that he is in the book. So they travel, and thare is some kind of fight, and I thought, yay, now we'll see some good, quality character interaction, and maybe author will permit us to get to know them all a bit. And then...kind-of-vampire and chick just go. Puff! Somewhere.<br />And that was the last straw. At that point I decided to make "couldn't finish" shelf, just to put this thing there.<br />Good luck if you decide to read it. I won't bother.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1747085229340280236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8328507563514568585">Don't let my low ranking deter you - this is a perfectly fine book, just not my exactly my personal cup of tea.<br/><br/>First off it has kind of a fairytale vibe for me - and I never liked those.<br/><br/>It also starts off with a feel like a secondary world - but after a short while (so no spoiler) we learn that it actually us humans in the future - and I personally HATE mix ups of realworld and secondary worlds. No idea why - it just doesn't click with me.<br/><br/>It is written emotionally - don't get me wrong, it isn't </span>
  <span id="freeText8328507563514568585" style="display:none">Don't let my low ranking deter you - this is a perfectly fine book, just not my exactly my personal cup of tea.<br /><br />First off it has kind of a fairytale vibe for me - and I never liked those.<br /><br />It also starts off with a feel like a secondary world - but after a short while (so no spoiler) we learn that it actually us humans in the future - and I personally HATE mix ups of realworld and secondary worlds. No idea why - it just doesn't click with me.<br /><br />It is written emotionally - don't get me wrong, it isn't a romance or anything, but I much prefer a style that is more matter of fact and way faster paced. <br /><br />So all these things don't make it a bad book at all - they just mean it isn't the perfect book for me!<br />The plot itself is interesting and the prose is fine, even if it isn't my favorite. Some of the characters could have had a bit more depth, but overall they were pretty well developed as well.<br /><br />So if you don't object to my pet peeves, this might still be the perfect book for you. :)</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2171812605644278644">This book started very promising. It has amazing worldbuilding, some interesting plot points (especially with the different religions and the magic vs. religion debate), and a few really interesting characters. <br/><br/>After a short while, though, a lot of things that Friedman was building is thrown out and it turns into your basic fantasy quest with lots and lots of walking around and our heroes bumbling blindly into dangerous situations. <br/><br/>It's a real shame, because Friedman could have done so much more</span>
  <span id="freeText2171812605644278644" style="display:none">This book started very promising. It has amazing worldbuilding, some interesting plot points (especially with the different religions and the magic vs. religion debate), and a few really interesting characters. <br /><br />After a short while, though, a lot of things that Friedman was building is thrown out and it turns into your basic fantasy quest with lots and lots of walking around and our heroes bumbling blindly into dangerous situations. <br /><br />It's a real shame, because Friedman could have done so much more with this amazing world than just using it as a backdrop for a banal fetch quest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2171812605644278644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_460239858" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460239858" />
    <a title="Blake Charlton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2698100-blake-charlton"><img alt="Blake Charlton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442492307p2/2698100.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460239858?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blake Charlton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blake Charlton" href="/user/show/2698100-blake-charlton">Blake Charlton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460239858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3820932389007029255">five stars for classic science fantasy with wonderful world building. vivid setting and characters, a straight-forward and satisfying story. my only complaint concerned anachronisms in the prose style (e.g. characters from a pseudo-medieval (or maybe pseudo-neogothic) culture using corporate slang like "PR"). but overall, this is a wonderful series and deserves to be revisited in this era of gritty fantasy. i'm looking for the rest of the series. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bgKevMd2iyg/UyIGn+M7FqNwD0yXuT8Y5sU0jWd2eFl4MpDarh9wbaX+kFaENZ+AnfMO46Catn4wpULk3009VA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Yxu1PSxD86VI2k92xndAB6pQn7XvAO+Bmu5TWCRWXXl1K7tbRSoI4NJ3/SbdoeSRlNOeGtgjZudMjiUxnG0YdA==')})
  }
